       </a>

       </a>

       <a href="/wiki/Surname" title="Surname">
        family name
       </a>
       is
       <i>
        Macaraeg
       </i>
       , the birth surname or paternal family name is
       <i>
        Macapagal
       </i>
       , and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Married_name" title="Married name">
        marital name
       </a>

         </a>
         <small>

         </small>
         <br/>

      <p>
       <b>
        Dr. Maria Gloria Macaraeg Macapagal-Arroyo, Ph.D.
       </b>
       (born April 5, 1947)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBIY_2-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CBIY-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       is a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino_people" title="Filipino people">
        Filipina
       </a>
       professor and politician who served as the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Presidents_of_the_Philippines" title="List of Presidents of the Philippines">
        14th President of the Philippines
       </a>
       from 2001 until 2010, as the
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Vice_Presidents_of_the_Philippines" title="List of Vice Presidents of the Philippines">
        10th Vice President of the Philippines
       </a>
       from 1998 to 2001, as the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deputy_speaker" title="Deputy speaker">
        deputy speaker
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_the_Philippines" title="Congress of the Philippines">
        17th Congress
       </a>
       and a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_the_Philippines" title="House of Representatives of the Philippines">
        House of Representatives
       </a>
       representing the
       <a href="/wiki/Legislative_districts_of_Pampanga#2nd_District" title="Legislative districts of Pampanga">
        2nd District
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Pampanga" title="Pampanga">
        Pampanga
       </a>
       since 2010. She was the country's second
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_elected_and_appointed_female_heads_of_state" title="List of elected and appointed female heads of state">
        female president
       </a>
       (after
       <a href="/wiki/Corazon_Aquino" title="Corazon Aquino">
        Corazon Aquino
       </a>
       ), and the daughter of former President
       <a href="/wiki/Diosdado_Macapagal" title="Diosdado Macapagal">
        Diosdado Macapagal
       </a>
       . Arroyo is also the first duly elected female Vice President of the Philippines.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         [3]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Arroyo was a former professor of economics at
       <a href="/wiki/Ateneo_de_Manila_University" title="Ateneo de Manila University">
        Ateneo de Manila University
       </a>
       where
       <a href="/wiki/Benigno_Aquino_III" title="Benigno Aquino III">
        Benigno Aquino III
       </a>
       was one of her students. She entered government in 1987, serving as assistant secretary and undersecretary of the
       <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Trade_and_Industry_(Philippines)" title="Department of Trade and Industry (Philippines)">
        Department of Trade and Industry
       </a>
       upon the invitation of President Corazon Aquino. After serving as a senator from 1992 to 1998, she was elected to the
       <a href="/wiki/Vice_President_of_the_Philippines" title="Vice President of the Philippines">
        vice presidency
       </a>
       under President
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Estrada" title="Joseph Estrada">
        Joseph Estrada
       </a>
       , despite having run on an opposing ticket.
      </p>
      <p>
       After Estrada was accused of corruption, she resigned her cabinet position as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_Social_Welfare_and_Development_(Philippines)" title="Department of Social Welfare and Development (Philippines)">
        Secretary of Social Welfare and Development
       </a>
       and joined the growing opposition to the president, who faced impeachment. Estrada was soon forced from office by the
       <a href="/wiki/EDSA_Revolution_of_2001" title="EDSA Revolution of 2001">
        EDSA Revolution of 2001
       </a>
       , and Arroyo was sworn into the presidency by Chief Justice
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hilario_Davide,_Jr." title="Hilario Davide, Jr.">
        Hilario Davide, Jr.
       </a>
       on January 20, 2001. She was elected to a full six-year presidential term in the controversial May
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_presidential_election,_2004" title="Philippine presidential election, 2004">
        2004 Philippine elections
       </a>
       , and was sworn in on June 30, 2004. Following her presidency, she was elected to the House of Representatives, making her the second Philippine president—after
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jose_P._Laurel" title="Jose P. Laurel">
        Jose P. Laurel
       </a>
       —to pursue a lower office after their presidency.
      </p>
      <p>
       On November 18, 2011, Arroyo was arrested following the filing of criminal charges against her for electoral fraud. She was held at the
       <a href="/wiki/Veterans_Memorial_Medical_Center" title="Veterans Memorial Medical Center">
        Veterans Memorial Medical Center
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">
        Quezon City
       </a>
       under charges of
       <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fraud" title="Electoral fraud">
        electoral sabotage
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vmmc_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-vmmc-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alvarez_5-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-alvarez-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but released on bail in July 2012. She was rearrested while in the hospital on charges of misuse of $8.8 million in state lottery funds in October 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         [6]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On July 19, 2016, after the public backing of president
       <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_Duterte" title="Rodrigo Duterte">
        Rodrigo Duterte
       </a>
       , she was acquitted by the
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines" title="Supreme Court of the Philippines">
        Supreme Court
       </a>
       by a vote of 11-4 despite numerous evidences pointing to her guilt.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         [7]
        </a>
       </sup>
       She has since been a member of the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Academy_of_the_Spanish_Language" title="Philippine Academy of the Spanish Language">
        Philippine Academy of the Spanish Language
       </a>
       after she announced her support to bring back Spanish as an official language of the Philippines during her presidency of 10 years. She, however, failed to do so.
      </p>
      <p>
      </p>

      <p>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">
        Early life
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       She was born as
       <b>
        Maria Gloria Macaraeg Macapagal
       </b>
       to politician
       <a href="/wiki/Diosdado_Macapagal" title="Diosdado Macapagal">
        Diosdado Macapagal
       </a>
       and his wife,
       <a href="/wiki/Eva_Macapagal" title="Eva Macapagal">
        Evangelina Macaraeg Macapagal
       </a>
       . She is the sister of Dr. Diosdado "Boboy" Macapagal, Jr. and Cielo Macapagal Salgado. She spent the first years of her life in
       <a href="/wiki/Lubao,_Pampanga" title="Lubao, Pampanga">
        Lubao, Pampanga
       </a>
       , with her two older siblings from her father's first marriage.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBIY_2-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-CBIY-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       At the age of four, she chose to live with her maternal grandmother in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Iligan_City" title="Iligan City">
        Iligan City
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time_8-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Time-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       She stayed there for three years, then split her time between
       <a href="/wiki/Mindanao" title="Mindanao">
        Mindanao
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Manila" title="Manila">
        Manila
       </a>
       until the age of 11.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Time_8-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Time-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       She is a skilled polyglot. She is fluent in English,
       <a href="/wiki/Tagalog_language" title="Tagalog language">
        Tagalog
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_language_in_the_Philippines" title="Spanish language in the Philippines">
        Spanish
       </a>
       , French, and several other Philippine languages, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Kapampangan_language" title="Kapampangan language">
        Kapampangan
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ilokano_language" title="Ilokano language">
        Ilokano
       </a>
       , Hiligaynon, Pangasinense, Bikolano, and
       <a href="/wiki/Cebuano_language" title="Cebuano language">
        Cebuano
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1961, when Arroyo was just 14 years old, her father was elected as president. She moved with her family into
       <a href="/wiki/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace" title="Malacañang Palace">
        Malacañang Palace
       </a>
       in Manila. A municipality was named in her honor,
       <a href="/wiki/Gloria,_Oriental_Mindoro" title="Gloria, Oriental Mindoro">
        Gloria, Oriental Mindoro
       </a>
       . She attended
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assumption_College_(Philippines)" title="Assumption College (Philippines)">
        Assumption Convent
       </a>
       for her elementary and high school education, graduating
       <a href="/wiki/Valedictorian" title="Valedictorian">
        valedictorian
       </a>
       in 1964. Arroyo then studied for two years at
       <a href="/wiki/Georgetown_University" title="Georgetown University">
        Georgetown University
       </a>
       's
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walsh_School_of_Foreign_Service" title="Walsh School of Foreign Service">
        Walsh School of Foreign Service
       </a>
       in Washington, D.C. where she was a classmate of future United States President
       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">
        Bill Clinton
       </a>
       and achieved consistent Dean's list status.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       She then earned her Bachelor of Arts degree in Economics from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Assumption_College_(Philippines)" title="Assumption College (Philippines)">
        Assumption College
       </a>
       , graduating
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Magna_cum_laude" title="Magna cum laude">
        magna cum laude
       </a>
       in 1968.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1968, Arroyo married lawyer and businessman
       <a href="/wiki/Jose_Miguel_Arroyo" title="Jose Miguel Arroyo">
        Jose Miguel Arroyo
       </a>
       of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Binalbagan,_Negros_Occidental" title="Binalbagan, Negros Occidental">
        Binalbagan, Negros Occidental
       </a>
       , whom she had met while still a teenager.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBIY_2-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-CBIY-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They had three children,
       <a href="/wiki/Mikey_Arroyo" title="Mikey Arroyo">
        Juan Miguel
       </a>
       (born 1969), Evangelina Lourdes (born 1971) and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Diosdado_Macapagal-Arroyo" title="Diosdado Macapagal-Arroyo">
        Diosdado Ignacio Jose Maria
       </a>
       (born in 1974). She pursued a master's degree in Economics at the
       <a href="/wiki/Ateneo_de_Manila_University" title="Ateneo de Manila University">
        Ateneo de Manila University
       </a>
       (1978) and a Ph.D. in Economics from the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_Philippines_Diliman" title="University of the Philippines Diliman">
        University of the Philippines Diliman
       </a>
       (1985).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-10">
         [10]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From 1977 to 1987, she held teaching positions in several schools, notably the University of the Philippines and the Ateneo de Manila University. She became chairperson of the Economics Department at Assumption College.
      </p>
      <p>
       In 1987, she was invited by President
       <a href="/wiki/Corazon_Aquino" title="Corazon Aquino">
        Corazon Aquino
       </a>
       to join the government as Assistant Secretary of the
       <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Trade_and_Industry_(Philippines)" title="Department of Trade and Industry (Philippines)">
        Department of Trade and Industry
       </a>
       . She was promoted to Undersecretary two years later. In her concurrent position as Executive Director of the Garments and Textile Export Board, Arroyo oversaw the rapid growth of the garment industry in the late 1980s.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Senator">
        Senator
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Senator">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Arroyo entered politics in the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Senate_election,_1992" title="Philippine Senate election, 1992">
        1992 election
       </a>
       , running for
       <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_the_Philippines" title="Senate of the Philippines">
        senator
       </a>
       . At the first general election under the 1987 Constitution, the top twelve vote-getting senatorial candidates would win a six-year term, and the next twelve candidates would win a three-year term.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Arroyo ranked 13th in the elections, earning a three-year term. She was
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Senate_election,_1995" title="Philippine Senate election, 1995">
        re-elected in 1995
       </a>
       , topping the senatorial election with nearly 16 million votes.
      </p>
      <p>
       As a legislator, Arroyo filed over 400 bills and authored or sponsored 55 laws during her tenure as senator, including the Anti-Sexual Harassment Law, the Indigenous People's Rights Law, and the Export Development Act.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CBIY_2-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-CBIY-2">
         [2]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The 1995 Mining Act, which allows 100% foreign ownership of Philippine mines, has come under fire from left-wing political groups.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Vice_Presidency">
        Vice Presidency
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Vice Presidency">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Arroyo considered a run for the presidency in the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_general_election,_1998" title="Philippine general election, 1998">
        1998 election
       </a>
       , but was persuaded by President
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fidel_V._Ramos" title="Fidel V. Ramos">
        Fidel V. Ramos
       </a>
       and leaders of the administration party
       <a href="/wiki/Lakas%E2%80%93CMD_(1991)" title="Lakas–CMD (1991)">
        Lakas-Christian Muslim Democrats
       </a>
       to instead seek the vice-presidency as the running mate of its presidential candidate, House Speaker
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jose_de_Venecia,_Jr." title="Jose de Venecia, Jr.">
        Jose de Venecia, Jr.
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malaya_12-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Malaya-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Though the latter lost to popular former actor
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Estrada" title="Joseph Estrada">
        Joseph Estrada
       </a>
       , Arroyo won the vice presidency by a large margin, garnering more than twice the votes of her closest opponent, Estrada's running mate Senator
       <a href="/wiki/Edgardo_Angara" title="Edgardo Angara">
        Edgardo Angara
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-presproj_13-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-presproj-13">
         [13]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Arroyo began her term as Vice President on June 30, 1998. She was appointed by Estrada to a concurrent position in the cabinet as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Department_of_Social_Welfare_and_Development_(Philippines)" title="Department of Social Welfare and Development (Philippines)">
        Secretary of Social Welfare and Development
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Malaya_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Malaya-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Arroyo resigned from the Cabinet in October 2000, distancing herself from Estrada, who was accused of corruption by a former political supporter,
       <a href="/wiki/Chavit_Singson" title="Chavit Singson">
        Chavit Singson
       </a>
       , Governor from Ilocos Sur.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sc_14-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-sc-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
       She had initially resisted pressure from allies to speak out against Estrada,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         [15]
        </a>
       </sup>
       but eventually joined calls for Estrada's resignation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sc_14-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-sc-14">
         [14]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Presidency">
        Presidency
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">

         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-BLP_sources" role="presentation">

       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo" title="Presidency of Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo">
        Presidency of Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span id="First_Term_.282001.E2.80.932004.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="First_Term_(2001–2004)">
        First Term (2001–2004)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: First Term (2001–2004)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Succession">
        Succession
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Succession">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       The last quarter of 2000 up to the first week of January 2001 was a period of political and economic uncertainty for the Philippines. On January 16, 2001, the impeachment trial also took a new direction. Private prosecutors walked out of the trial when pro-Estrada senators prevented the opening of an evidence (a brown envelope) containing bank records allegedly owned by President Estrada. With the walkout, the impeachment trial was not completed and Filipinos eventually took to the streets in masses to continue the clamor for President Estrada's resignation. From January 17 to 20, 2001,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2001_EDSA_Revolution" title="2001 EDSA Revolution">
        hundreds of thousands
       </a>
       of Filipinos gathered at
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epifanio_de_los_Santos_Avenue" title="Epifanio de los Santos Avenue">
        Epifanio de los Santos Avenue
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/EDSA_(road)" title="EDSA (road)">
        EDSA
       </a>
       ), the site of the original
       <a href="/wiki/People_Power_Revolution" title="People Power Revolution">
        People Power Revolution
       </a>
       . The clamor for a change in the presidency gained momentum as various sectors of Philippine society – professionals, students, artists, politicians, leftist and rightist groups – joined what became known as EDSA II. Officials of the administration, the
       <a href="/wiki/Armed_Forces_of_the_Philippines" title="Armed Forces of the Philippines">
        Armed Forces of the Philippines
       </a>
       (AFP), and the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_National_Police" title="Philippine National Police">
        Philippine National Police
       </a>
       (PNP) also withdrew their support for President Estrada.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Php_bill_200_back.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="379" data-file-width="947" height="90" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Php_bill_200_back.jpg/225px-Php_bill_200_back.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Php_bill_200_back.jpg/338px-Php_bill_200_back.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6f/Php_bill_200_back.jpg/450px-Php_bill_200_back.jpg 2x" width="225"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Php_bill_200_back.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Gloria Macapagal Arroyo displayed on a
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_two_hundred_peso_bill" title="Philippine two hundred peso bill">
          two hundred peso bill
         </a>
         , being sworn in as president by Chief Justice Hilario Davide, Jr. in January 2001.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Days after leaving
       <a href="/wiki/Malaca%C3%B1ang_Palace" title="Malacañang Palace">
        Malacañang Palace
       </a>
       , President Estrada's lawyers questioned the legitimacy of Arroyo's presidency before the Supreme Court. He reiterated that he had not resigned as president and that at most, Arroyo was just serving in an acting capacity. The high court, however, voted unanimously to uphold the legitimacy of Arroyo's succession. As a consequence, Estrada no longer enjoys immunity from charges being filed against him.
      </p>
      <p>
       In the last week of April 2001, the Sandiganbayan ordered the arrest of Estrada and his son, then mayor
       <a href="/wiki/Jinggoy_Estrada" title="Jinggoy Estrada">
        Jinggoy Estrada
       </a>
       , for plunder charges. A few days later, Estrada supporters protested his arrest, gathered at the EDSA Shrine, and staged what they called,
       <a href="/wiki/EDSA_III" title="EDSA III">
        EDSA III
       </a>
       – comparing their actions to the People Power revolution of 1986 and January 2001.
      </p>
      <p>
       Thousands of protesters demanded the release of Estrada. Eventually, they also called for the ouster of Arroyo and the reinstatement of the former. On May 1, 2001, they marched towards Malacañang to force Arroyo to give in to their demands. Violence erupted when the protesters attempted to storm the presidential palace and the military and police were ordered to use their arms to drive them back. Arroyo declared a state of rebellion because of the violence and prominent political personalities affiliated with Estrada were charged and arrested. The so-called EDSA III was the first serious political challenge to the Arroyo presidency.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Corruption_charges_and_Oakwood_Mutiny">
        Corruption charges and Oakwood Mutiny
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Corruption charges and Oakwood Mutiny">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Oakwood_mutiny" title="Oakwood mutiny">
        Oakwood mutiny
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Oakwood mutiny occurred in the Philippines on July 27, 2003. A group of 321 armed soldiers who called themselves "
       <i>
        Bagong Katipuneros
       </i>
       "
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-laurel_16-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-laurel-16">
         [16]
        </a>
       </sup>
       led by Army Capt. Gerardo Gambala and Lt.
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antonio_Trillanes_IV" title="Antonio Trillanes IV">
        Antonio Trillanes IV
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_Navy" title="Philippine Navy">
        Philippine Navy
       </a>
       took over the Oakwood Premier Ayala Center (now Ascott Makati) serviced apartment tower in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Makati_City" title="Makati City">
        Makati City
       </a>
       to show the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Filipino_people" title="Filipino people">
        Filipino people
       </a>
       the alleged corruption of the Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo administration. They also stated that they saw signs suggesting that the President was going to declare
       <a href="/wiki/Martial_law" title="Martial law">
        martial law
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Later in 2011, after being ousted from presidency, Arroyo was charged with
       <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fraud" title="Electoral fraud">
        electoral fraud
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Corruption_in_the_Philippines" title="Corruption in the Philippines">
        corruption
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         [17]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2004_Presidential_Election">
        2004 Presidential Election
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2004 Presidential Election">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em">
       <tr>
        <th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold;font-weight: normal; background-color: #DEDEDE;">
         <span style="font-size:80%">
          Presidential styles of
         </span>
         <br/>
         <b>
          <span class="fn">
           Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo
          </span>
         </b>
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td colspan="2" style="text-align:center">
         <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Philippines.svg">
          <img alt="Seal of the President of the Philippines.svg" data-file-height="2425" data-file-width="2424" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Philippines.svg/50px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Philippines.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Philippines.svg/75px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Philippines.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Philippines.svg/100px-Seal_of_the_President_of_the_Philippines.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         <a href="/wiki/Style_(manner_of_address)" title="Style (manner of address)">
          Reference style
         </a>
        </th>
        <td>
         <a href="/wiki/Excellency" title="Excellency">
          Her Excellency
         </a>
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         Spoken style
        </th>
        <td>
         Your Excellency
        </td>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <th scope="row">
         Alternative style
        </th>
        <td>
         Madam President
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       Article VII Section 4 of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1987_Constitution" title="1987 Constitution">
        1987 Constitution
       </a>
       explicitly states that the president of the Philippines can only serve for one term. However, the same provision also implicitly states that a president's successor who has not served for more than four years can still seek a full term for the presidency. Although Arroyo fell under this category, she initially announced on December 30, 2002 that she would not seek the presidency in 2004. She emphasized that she would devote her remaining months in office to serving the people and improving the economy of the Philippines.
      </p>
      <p>
       In October 2003, Arroyo changed her mind and announced that she would contest the May 2004 presidential elections and seek a direct mandate from the people. She explained, "There is a higher cause to change society...in a way that nourishes our future". With her decision, the initial criticisms hurled against Arroyo centered on her lack of word of honor.
      </p>
      <p>
       As predicted by SWS exit polls, Arroyo won the election by a margin of over one million votes against Poe. However, the congressional canvassing was quite contentious as opposition lawmakers in the National Board of Canvassers argued that there were many discrepancies in the election returns and that insinuations of cheating were raised. On June 23, 2004, Congress proclaimed Arroyo and
       <a href="/wiki/Noli_de_Castro" title="Noli de Castro">
        Noli de Castro
       </a>
       as president and vice president, respectively.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span id="Second_Term_.282004.E2.80.932010.29">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Second_Term_(2004–2010)">
        Second Term (2004–2010)
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Second Term (2004–2010)">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2004_Presidential_Election_rigging_allegations">
        2004 Presidential Election rigging allegations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2004 Presidential Election rigging allegations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arroyo_inauguration.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="243" data-file-width="316" height="173" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7c/Arroyo_inauguration.jpg/225px-Arroyo_inauguration.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/7/7c/Arroyo_inauguration.jpg 1.5x" width="225"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arroyo_inauguration.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Arroyo taking her Oath of Office for a full term as president before Chief Justice
         <a href="/wiki/Hilario_Davide_Jr." title="Hilario Davide Jr.">
          Hilario Davide Jr.
         </a>
         in
         <a href="/wiki/Cebu_City" title="Cebu City">
          Cebu City
         </a>
         on June 30, 2004.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On June 30, 2004, in a break with tradition, Arroyo first delivered her inaugural speech at the
       <a href="/wiki/Quirino_Grandstand" title="Quirino Grandstand">
        Quirino Grandstand
       </a>
       in Manila. She then departed for
       <a href="/wiki/Cebu_City" title="Cebu City">
        Cebu City
       </a>
       for her oath taking, the first time that a Philippine president took the oath of office outside of
       <a href="/wiki/Luzon" title="Luzon">
        Luzon
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Allegations of cheating against Arroyo gained momentum one year after the May 2004 elections. In a press conference held on June 10, 2005,
       <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Ong" title="Samuel Ong">
        Samuel Ong
       </a>
       , former deputy director of the
       <a href="/wiki/National_Bureau_of_Investigation_(Philippines)" title="National Bureau of Investigation (Philippines)">
        National Bureau of Investigation
       </a>
       (NBI) claimed to have audio recordings of wiretapped conversations between Arroyo and an official of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Commission_on_Elections" title="Commission on Elections">
        Commission on Elections
       </a>
       (COMELEC).
       <a href="/wiki/Virgilio_Garcillano" title="Virgilio Garcillano">
        Virgilio Garcillano
       </a>
       , a former COMELEC commissioner, would later be identified as the official talking to Arroyo. According to Ong, the recordings allegedly proved that Arroyo ordered the rigging of the national elections for her to win by around one million votes against Poe.
      </p>
      <p>
       The recordings of Ong became known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Hello_Garci_scandal" title="Hello Garci scandal">
        Hello Garci controversy
       </a>
       and triggered massive protests against Arroyo. Key members of her cabinet resigned from their respective posts and urged Arroyo to do the same. On June 27, 2005, Arroyo admitted to inappropriately speaking to a COMELEC official, claiming it was a "lapse in judgement". She, however, denied influencing the outcome of the elections and declared that she won the elections fairly. Arroyo did not resign despite the pressures coming from various sectors of society.
      </p>
      <p>
       The Hello Garci controversy became the basis of the impeachment case filed against Arroyo in 2005. Attempts to impeach Arroyo failed later that year. Another impeachment case was filed against Arroyo in 2006 but was also defeated at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_House_of_Representatives" title="Philippine House of Representatives">
        House of Representatives
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In October 2007, lawyer Alan Paguia filed an impeachment complaint against Arroyo in connection with the issue of bribery. Paguia's complaint was based on the revelation of
       <a href="/wiki/Pampanga" title="Pampanga">
        Pampanga
       </a>
       Governor
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ed_Panlilio" title="Ed Panlilio">
        Ed Panlilio
       </a>
       that various governors received half a million pesos from Malacañang. The impeachment case, as of the middle of October 2007, has already been referred to the House of Representatives Committee on Justice.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="State_of_Emergency">
        State of Emergency
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: State of Emergency">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/2006_state_of_emergency_in_the_Philippines" title="2006 state of emergency in the Philippines">
        2006 state of emergency in the Philippines
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-5.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="334" data-file-width="500" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-5.jpg/220px-Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-5.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-5.jpg/330px-Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-5.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-5.jpg/440px-Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-5.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Dmitry_Medvedev_5_June_2009-5.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         President Arroyo with Russian President
         <a href="/wiki/Dmitry_Medvedev" title="Dmitry Medvedev">
          Dmitry Medvedev
         </a>
         , June 9, 2009
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       On February 24, 2006, a plot to take over the government was uncovered by authorities, allegedly headed by Gen.
       <a href="/wiki/Danilo_Lim" title="Danilo Lim">
        Danilo Lim
       </a>
       and other rightist military adventurists. General Lim and some of his men were arrested. To face the threat posed by enemies of the state, Arroyo issued Presidential Proclamation 1017 (PP 1017) and used it as basis in declaring a state of emergency throughout the Philippines. According to Arroyo, this declaration was done to quell the military rebellion, stop lawless violence, and promote peace and stability. PP 1017 also empowered the government to enforce warrantless arrests and take over strategic private utilities companies.
      </p>
      <p>
       On February 25, 2006, the police raided the office of the
       <i>
        Daily Tribune
       </i>
       , a newspaper known as a critic of the Arroyo administration. The government then issued a journalism guidelines to address the threat posed by critics in the media. Presidential Management Staff chief
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Michael_Defensor" title="Michael Defensor">
        Michael Defensor
       </a>
       said that the guidelines were necessary in order to cope with the emergency situation.
      </p>
      <p>
       The state of emergency existed for about one week with the purpose of curbing further violence, illegal rallies, and public disturbance throughout the Philippines. The police and the military dispersed demonstrators and protesters, especially those along
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epifanio_de_los_Santos_Avenue" title="Epifanio de los Santos Avenue">
        Epifanio de los Santos Avenue
       </a>
       (EDSA). Aside from General Lim, prominent personalities were also arrested in connection with their alleged participation in the attempt to overthrow the government. Among those arrested were:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        Col. Ariel Querubin – leader of a group of
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Marines" title="Philippine Marines">
         Philippine Marines
        </a>
        who engaged the government in a political stand-off at
        <a href="/wiki/Fort_Bonifacio" title="Fort Bonifacio">
         Fort Bonifacio
        </a>
        on February 25, 2005
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Randy_David" title="Randy David">
         Randy David
        </a>
        – led a protest rally without securing the necessary permit
       </li>
       <li>
        <a href="/wiki/Crispin_Beltran" title="Crispin Beltran">
         Crispin Beltran
        </a>
        – party-list representative of
        <a href="/wiki/Anakpawis" title="Anakpawis">
         Anakpawis
        </a>
        charged with inciting to sedition and rebellion
       </li>
       <li>
        Batasan Five – party-list representatives charged with rebellion and were placed under the custody of the House of Representatives;
        <a href="/wiki/Bayan_Muna" title="Bayan Muna">
         Bayan Muna
        </a>
        's
        <a href="/wiki/Teodoro_Casi%C3%B1o" title="Teodoro Casiño">
         Teodoro Casiño
        </a>
        ,
        <a href="/wiki/Satur_Ocampo" title="Satur Ocampo">
         Satur Ocampo
        </a>
        , and
        <a href="/wiki/Joel_Virador" title="Joel Virador">
         Joel Virador
        </a>
        ;
        <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Women%27s_Party" title="Gabriela Women's Party">
         Gabriela
        </a>
        's
        <a href="/wiki/Liza_Maza" title="Liza Maza">
         Liza Maza
        </a>
        , and Anakpawis'
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rafael_Mariano" title="Rafael Mariano">
         Rafael Mariano
        </a>
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       PP 1017 was lifted on March 3, 2006 but members of the opposition, private lawyers, and concerned citizens challenged its constitutionality before the Supreme Court. On May 4, the high court declared the proclamation constitutional. However, it also said that it was illegal for the government to implement warrantless arrests and seize private institutions and companies.
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Charter_Change">
        Charter Change
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Charter Change">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       Arroyo currently spearheads a controversial plan for an overhaul of the constitution to transform the present unitary and presidential republic with a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bicameral_legislature" title="Bicameral legislature">
        bicameral legislature
       </a>
       into a federal parliamentary government with a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Unicameral_legislature" title="Unicameral legislature">
        unicameral legislature
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">
        <a href="#cite_note-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:George_W._Bush_%26_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_in_the_Oval_Office_2003-05-19.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="396" data-file-width="264" height="330" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/George_W._Bush_%26_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_in_the_Oval_Office_2003-05-19.jpg/220px-George_W._Bush_%26_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_in_the_Oval_Office_2003-05-19.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f7/George_W._Bush_%26_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_in_the_Oval_Office_2003-05-19.jpg 1.5x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:George_W._Bush_%26_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_in_the_Oval_Office_2003-05-19.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         President Arroyo with U.S. President
         <a href="/wiki/George_W._Bush" title="George W. Bush">
          George W. Bush
         </a>
         , May 19, 2003
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">
        Economy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Economy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo#Economy" title="Presidency of Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo">
        Presidency of Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo § Economy
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Arroyo, who earned a master's degree and doctorate in economics, made the
       <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Philippines" title="Economy of the Philippines">
        Philippine economy
       </a>
       the focus of her presidency. Annual economic growth in the Philippines averaged 4.5% during the Arroyo administration, expanding every quarter of her presidency.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ciaf_19-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ciaf-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This is higher than in the administrations of her three immediate predecessors,
       <a href="/wiki/Corazon_Aquino" title="Corazon Aquino">
        Corazon Aquino
       </a>
       (3.8%),
       <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Ramos" title="Fidel Ramos">
        Fidel Ramos
       </a>
       (3.7%), and
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Estrada" title="Joseph Estrada">
        Joseph Estrada
       </a>
       (3.7%).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         [20]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Philippine economy grew at its fastest pace in three decades in 2007, with real GDP growth exceeding 7%.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         [21]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The economy was one of the few to avoid contraction during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Financial_crisis_(2007%E2%80%93present)" title="Financial crisis (2007–present)">
        2008 global financial crisis
       </a>
       , faring better than its regional peers due to minimal exposure to troubled international securities, lower dependence on exports, relatively resilient domestic consumption, large remittances from four-to five-million overseas Filipino workers, and a growing business process outsourcing industry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ciaf_19-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ciaf-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Arroyo's handling of the economy has earned praise from former US President
       <a href="/wiki/Bill_Clinton" title="Bill Clinton">
        Bill Clinton
       </a>
       , who cited her "tough decisions" that put the Philippine economy back in shape.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">
        <a href="#cite_note-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Despite this growth, the poverty rate remained stagnant due to a high population growth rate and uneven distribution of income.
      </p>
      <p>
       A controversial expanded
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Value_added_tax" title="Value added tax">
        value added tax
       </a>
       (e-VAT) law, considered the centerpiece of the Arroyo administration's economic reform agenda, was implemented in November 2005, aiming to complement revenue-raising efforts that could plug the country's large budget deficit.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Her administration originally set a target to balance the national budget by 2010. The tax measure boosted confidence in the government's fiscal capacity and helped to strengthen the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_peso" title="Philippine peso">
        Philippine peso
       </a>
       , making it East Asia's best performing currency in 2005–06.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The peso strengthened by nearly 20% in 2007, making it one of Asia's better performing currencies for that year, a fact attributed to a combination of increased remittances from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Overseas_Filipino_workers" title="Overseas Filipino workers">
        overseas Filipino workers
       </a>
       and a strong domestic economy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25">
        <a href="#cite_note-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Early in her presidency, Arroyo implemented a controversial policy of holiday economics, adjusting holidays to form longer weekends with the purpose of boosting domestic tourism and allowing Filipinos more time with their families.
      </p>
      <p>
       The rate of inflation during the later portion of Arroyo's administration was so high. Common consumer goods became prohibitive in cost. There was a marked decrease in the number of students in universities. Privately owned universities closed in numbers.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="Reliable source needed for the whole sentence (May 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hillary_Clinton_with_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_2-6-09.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="398" data-file-width="600" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Hillary_Clinton_with_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_2-6-09.jpg/220px-Hillary_Clinton_with_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_2-6-09.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Hillary_Clinton_with_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_2-6-09.jpg/330px-Hillary_Clinton_with_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_2-6-09.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/Hillary_Clinton_with_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_2-6-09.jpg/440px-Hillary_Clinton_with_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_2-6-09.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hillary_Clinton_with_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_2-6-09.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         President Arroyo with U.S. Secretary of State
         <a href="/wiki/Hillary_Clinton" title="Hillary Clinton">
          Hillary Clinton
         </a>
         , February 17, 2009
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>

       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo#Domestic_policies" title="Presidency of Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo">

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_policies">
        Foreign policies
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Foreign policies">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Presidency_of_Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo#Foreign_Policies" title="Presidency of Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo">
        Presidency of Gloria Macapagal-Arroyo § Foreign Policies
       </a>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Public_perception">
        Public perception
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Public perception">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_net_satisfaction.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="425" data-file-width="800" height="159" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_net_satisfaction.png/300px-Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_net_satisfaction.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_net_satisfaction.png/450px-Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_net_satisfaction.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_net_satisfaction.png/600px-Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_net_satisfaction.png 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gloria_Macapagal-Arroyo_net_satisfaction.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Social Weather Stations quarterly public opinion polling of the net satisfaction rating of President Arroyo.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Social_Weather_Stations" title="Social Weather Stations">
        Social Weather Stations
       </a>
       public opinion group has conducted quarterly surveys tracking the net satisfaction rating ("satisfied" rating minus "dissatisfied" rating") of President Arroyo. She began her presidency in the first quarter of 2001 with a net satisfaction rating of +24. Her rating first dipped into the negative in the first quarter of 2003, making Arroyo the only president to achieve a negative net satisfaction rating in SWS opinion polling. Her rating rebounded well into the positive in 2004, in time for the presidential election where she won election to a new six-year term. However, net satisfaction sunk back into negative territory in the fourth quarter of 2004, and has remained negative since, dipping as low as −38 in the second quarter of 2008. Her net satisfaction rating in the first quarter of 2009 was −32.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26">
        <a href="#cite_note-26">
         [26]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Post-presidency">
        Post-presidency
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Post-presidency">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2009_biopsy">
        2009 biopsy
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 2009 biopsy">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       On July 3, 2009, it was announced that Arroyo had undergone a biopsy to examine lumps discovered in her breast and groin.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mb09_27-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mb09-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pdi09_28-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pdi09-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Press Secretary
       <a href="/wiki/Cerge_Remonde" title="Cerge Remonde">
        Cerge Remonde
       </a>
       stated that the results of the biopsy were negative.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mb09_27-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mb09-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pdi09_28-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-pdi09-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Remonde also denied reports published in the July 3, 2009 editions of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Manila_Bulletin" title="Manila Bulletin">
         Manila Bulletin
        </a>
       </i>
       and the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Philippine_Star" title="Philippine Star">
         Philippine Star
        </a>
       </i>
       that Arroyo had undergone surgery for the removal or repair of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breast_implants" title="Breast implants">
        breast silicone implants
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mb09_27-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-mb09-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pdi09_28-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-pdi09-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2010_election_to_House_of_Representatives">
        2010 election to House of Representatives
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 2010 election to House of Representatives">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In November 2009, Arroyo formally declared her intention to run for a seat in the
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_the_Philippines" title="House of Representatives of the Philippines">
        House of Representatives
       </a>
       representing the
       <a href="/wiki/Legislative_districts_of_Pampanga#2nd_District" title="Legislative districts of Pampanga">
        2nd District
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Pampanga" title="Pampanga">
        Pampanga
       </a>
       , making her the second Philippine President – after
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jose_P._Laurel" title="Jose P. Laurel">
        Jose P. Laurel
       </a>
       – to pursue a lower office after the expiration of their presidency.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-house1_30-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-house1-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A petition seeking to disqualify Arroyo from the race was dismissed by the
       <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_Elections_(Philippines)" title="Commission on Elections (Philippines)">
        Comelec
       </a>
       for lack of merit, a decision which was later affirmed by the Supreme Court.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       With little serious competition, she was elected to congress in May 2010 with a landslide victory.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
       After receiving final military honors at the inauguration ceremony of incoming President
       <a href="/wiki/Benigno_Aquino_III" title="Benigno Aquino III">
        Benigno Aquino III
       </a>
       , she headed straight to Pampanga for her own oath-taking as congresswoman.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Despite being considered the strongest contender for
       <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_House_of_Representatives_of_the_Philippines" title="Speaker of the House of Representatives of the Philippines">
        Speaker of the House
       </a>
       , Arroyo declined to seek the position, hoping instead to take on a role similar to
       <a href="/wiki/Sonia_Gandhi" title="Sonia Gandhi">
        Sonia Gandhi
       </a>
       , who was influential as merely the head of her party.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On her first day as a lawmaker, Arroyo and her son Dato filed a resolution calling for Congress to call a
       <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_convention_(political_meeting)" title="Constitutional convention (political meeting)">
        constitutional convention
       </a>
       to propose amendments to the existing constitution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2011_Spinal_surgery">
        2011 Spinal surgery
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 2011 Spinal surgery">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In early 2011 she was diagnosed with cervical spondylosis or cervical
       <a href="/wiki/Radiculopathy" title="Radiculopathy">
        radiculopathy
       </a>
       . She was rushed to the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=St._Luke%27s_Medical_Center_%E2%80%93_Global_City&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="St. Luke's Medical Center – Global City (page does not exist)">
        St. Luke's Medical Center
       </a>
       in Global City
       <a href="/wiki/Taguig" title="Taguig">
        Taguig
       </a>
       July 25, 2011, minutes after the State of the Nation Address by
       <a href="/wiki/Benigno_Aquino_III" title="Benigno Aquino III">
        Benigno Aquino III
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Doctors performed a 5-hour spine surgery on July 29, 2011
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Two more surgeries occurred in August 2011 which aggravated her
       <a href="/wiki/Hypoparathyroidism" title="Hypoparathyroidism">
        hypoparathyroidism
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/House_of_Representatives_of_the_Philippines" title="House of Representatives of the Philippines">
        House of Representatives
       </a>
       under the leadership of Speaker
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Feliciano_Belmonte,_Jr." title="Feliciano Belmonte, Jr.">
        Feliciano Belmonte, Jr.
       </a>
       issued a travel permit allowing her to have treatment in Germany despite the Department of Justice hold departure order.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2011_hospital_arrest">
        2011 hospital arrest
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 2011 hospital arrest">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Arroyo was arrested on November 18, 2011 after a
       <a href="/wiki/Pasay" title="Pasay">
        Pasay
       </a>
       court issued a warrant of arrest against her, following the filing of a complaint for electoral sabotage by the
       <a href="/wiki/Commission_on_Elections_(Philippines)" title="Commission on Elections (Philippines)">
        Commission on Elections
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The arrest warrant was served at a
       <a href="/wiki/St._Luke%27s_Medical_Center" title="St. Luke's Medical Center">
        St. Luke's Medical Center
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/Taguig" title="Taguig">
        Taguig
       </a>
       where Arroyo had been confined.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Days earlier, the
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines" title="Supreme Court of the Philippines">
        Supreme Court
       </a>
       had issued a Resolution enjoining attempts by the
       <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Justice_(Philippines)" title="Department of Justice (Philippines)">
        Department of Justice
       </a>
       to prevent her departure from the Philippines to seek medical treatment overseas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       She was transferred to the
       <a href="/wiki/Veterans_Memorial_Medical_Center" title="Veterans Memorial Medical Center">
        Veterans Memorial Medical Center
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Quezon_City" title="Quezon City">
        Quezon City
       </a>
       on December 9, 2011.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vmmc_4-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-vmmc-4">
         [4]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-alvarez_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-alvarez-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Arroyo was released from hospital arrest on bail on July 25, 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       On October 29, 2012, she refused to enter any
       <a href="/wiki/Plea" title="Plea">
        plea
       </a>
       on charges she misused $8.8 million in
       <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">
        state
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Lottery" title="Lottery">
        lottery
       </a>
       funds during her term in
       <a href="/wiki/Office" title="Office">
        office
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of December 2013, she was still in custody at the Veterans Memorial Medical Center.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
       On July 19, 2016 the Supreme Court dismissed the corruption charges and ordered her release from the hospital where she had been detained since 2012.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2013_reelection_to_House_of_Representatives">
        2013 reelection to House of Representatives
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 2013 reelection to House of Representatives">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       While still confined in the Veterans Medical Center, Arroyo successfully earned a second term as congresswoman for Pampanga's second legislative district at the conclusion of the
       <a href="/wiki/Philippine_general_election,_2013" title="Philippine general election, 2013">
        2013 Philippine mid-term elections
       </a>
       on 13 May 2013, defeating the ruling
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Liberal_Party_of_the_Philippines" title="Liberal Party of the Philippines">
        Liberal Party's
       </a>
       Vivian Dabu who was the provincial administrator under priest-turned-politician former Governor
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ed_Panlilio" title="Ed Panlilio">
        Among Ed Panlilio
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2014_medical_problems_and_reapplication_for_bail">
        2014 medical problems and reapplication for bail
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: 2014 medical problems and reapplication for bail">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Arroyo was transported to St. Luke's Medical Center for tests and treatment and returned to confinement at the Veteran's Medical Center after medical incidents in May and June 2014.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50">
        <a href="#cite_note-50">
         [50]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In June, after the second of these incidents, her attorneys renewed application for bail.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51">
        <a href="#cite_note-51">
         [51]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In September, a third medical incident caused her to again be rushed to St. Luke's for treatment and returned to confinement at the Veteran's Medical Center.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="2016_Supreme_Court_acquittal">
        2016 Supreme Court acquittal
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: 2016 Supreme Court acquittal">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       During the 2016 presidential campaign, then-candidate
       <a href="/wiki/Rodrigo_Duterte" title="Rodrigo Duterte">
        Rodrigo Duterte
       </a>
       announced his support for Arroyo's release from hospital arrest. On July 19, 2016, a few weeks after Duterte was sworn in as president, the
       <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_Philippines" title="Supreme Court of the Philippines">
        Supreme Court
       </a>
       ruled in favor of the dismissal of plunder case against Arroyo despite massive evidences pointing to her guilt, gathering a vote of 11-4 which was read by spokesperson Theodore Te. Seven of the 11 judges who voted for acquittal were appointed by Arroyo and three of the four justices who voted against Arroyo's acquittal were appointees of former President
       <a href="/wiki/Benigno_Aquino_III" title="Benigno Aquino III">
        Benigno Aquino III
       </a>
       , including Chief Justice
       <a href="/wiki/Maria_Lourdes_Sereno" title="Maria Lourdes Sereno">
        Maria Lourdes Sereno
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       She would later be assigned by Duterte's party, PDP-Laban, as a high-level member of the House of Representatives after winning her 3rd term as congresswoman in the House. She was given committee chairmanships, among many other roles.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Scouting">
        Scouting
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Scouting">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       Arroyo is the Chief Girl Scout of the
       <a href="/wiki/Girl_Scouts_of_the_Philippines" title="Girl Scouts of the Philippines">
        Girl Scouts of the Philippines
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_political_titles">
        Government and political titles
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Government and political titles">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <ul>
       <li>
        Undersecretary of Trade and Industry (1987–1992)
       </li>
       <li>
        Senator (1992–1998)
       </li>
       <li>
        Secretary of Social Welfare and Development (1998–2000)
       </li>
       <li>
        Vice President of the Philippines (1998–2001)
       </li>
       <li>
        President of the Philippines (2001–2010)
       </li>
       <li>
        Representative (2010–present)
       </li>
      </ul>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Patrilineal_descent">
        Patrilineal descent
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Gloria_Macapagal_Arroyo&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Patrilineal descent">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <table class="collapsible collapsed" style="margin: 0.3em auto auto; clear:none; min-width:70em; width:auto; font-size:88%; border:1px solid #aaa;">
       <tr>
        <th style="padding:0.2em 0.3em 0.2em 4.3em;background:none; width:auto">
         Patrilineal descent
        </th>
       </tr>
       <tr>
        <td style="text-align:left">
         <p>
          Arroyo's patriline is the line from which she is descended father to son.
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Patrilineal_descent" title="Patrilineal descent">
           Patrilineal descent
          </a>
          is the principle behind membership in royal houses, as it can be traced back through the generations—which means that if Arroyo were to choose an historically accurate house name it would be
          <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Tondo" title="Kingdom of Tondo">
           Kingdom of Tondo
          </a>
          . (Note: sharif/syarif and ibn/bin are of similar usage.)
         </p>
         <ol>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Abraham" title="Abraham">
            Abraham
           </a>
           (Ibrahim), around 2nd millennium BCE
          </li>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Ishmael" title="Ishmael">
            Ishmael
           </a>
           (Ismail), 1720 BCE-1580 BCE
          </li>
          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Hadad_(Bible)" title="Hadad (Bible)">
            Hadar
           </a>
          </li>
          <li>
           Aram, date unknown
          </li>
          <li>
           'Adwa, date unknown
          </li>
          <li>
           Wazzi, date unknown
          </li>
          <li>
           Sami, date unknown
          </li>
          <li>
           Zarih, date unknown
          </li>
          <li>
           Nahith, date unknown
          </li>
          <li>
           Muksar, date unknown
          </li>
          <li>
           Aiham, date unknown
          </li>

           Afnad, date unknown
          </li>

          </li>

          </li>

          </li>

          </li>

          </li>

          </li>

          </li>

          </li>

          </li>

          </li>

          <li>
           <a href="/wiki/Adnan" title="Adnan">
            Adnan bin Udd
           </a>
